<P style="margin:0pt" align=center><B>PART I</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt"><B>Item 1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; BUSINESS.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt"><B>Corporate History</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>SoOum Corp. (2015 to Present), (f/k/a Swordfish Financial, Inc., (2009-2015) (f/k/a Photo Control Corporation (1959-2004) and Nature Vision, Inc. (2004-2009)) (the &#147;Company&#148;, &#147;we,&#148; or &#147;us&#148;) was incorporated as a Minnesota corporation on August 19, 1959.&nbsp;&nbsp;On August 31, 2004, the Company changed its name to Nature Vision, Inc. in connection with a merger transaction with Nature Vision Operating Inc. (f/k/a Nature Vision, Inc.) a Minnesota corporation that was incorporated in 1998. As a part of the merger, Nature Vision Operating Inc. became a wholly-owned subsidiary of the Company. Upon the merger with Swordfish Financial, Inc., a Texas corporation on August 17, 2009, the shareholders of the Company owning a majority of the outstanding common stock voted to change the Company&#146;s name to Swordfish Financial, Inc.&nbsp;&nbsp; On November 12, 2014, SoOum, Corp., (&#147;SoOum&#148;) a Delaware corporation merged into the Company and on May 2, 2015 the shareholders voted to change the Company&#146;s name to SoOum Corp. &nbsp;Our executive offices are located at P.O. Box 431, Vernon, Arizona 85940; our telephone number is (646) 801-3772; and our website is <FONT COLOR=#0000FF><U>www.sooum.com</U></FONT>. </P>
<P style="margin-top:11pt; margin-bottom:0pt" align=justify>The Company is an international commodity trading arbitrage firm, which uses its own proprietary technology to identify and exploit arbitrage opportunities. &nbsp;The Company performs arbitrage on a defined supply and demand conditions creating price discrepancies of physical commodities in opposing markets. &nbsp;The Company also plans to distribute trade intelligence to global subscribers in order to solve supply shortages and to bring new business to local manufacturers. &nbsp;This part of the business is in the development stage. &nbsp;Unlike specialized supply chains, the Company&#146;s solutions focus on broad, real time information management, reliable trade economics, fast computing and proprietary algorithms to find surpluses and fill shortages. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt">The Company takes a coordinated view of the global economy seeking out predictability within the global flow of commodities and finding the Company&#146;s strategic position within that dynamic. Then, the Company implements tactics from the ancient persistence hunt model (hereafter &#147;PHM&#148;) to manage a pool of projects and brings a portion of these potential transactions to closing.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><BR></P>
<br><br>
<P align="center" style="line-height:13pt; margin:0pt; font-size:11pt; align=center;page-break-before:always">2</P>

<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><BR></P>
<P align="left" style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><b>Opportunity in Arbitrage Model</b></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=center><img src="soumtest001.jpg" alt="[soumtest001.jpg]" align=middle height=233.933 width=391.067></P>
<P style="line-height:13.5pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=center><B>Commodities</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13.5pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt">The Company primarily focuses on commodities highly demanded in areas of conflict and frontier marketplaces. The Company categorizes transactions as soft commodity trades and hard commodity trades.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt; padding-left:36pt; text-indent:54pt; font-size:10pt" align=justify>- <B><I>Soft Commodities Trades:</I></B> rice, wheat, sugar, soybeans, meats, live cattle, seafood, live seafood and other soft commodities, as intelligence indicates.</P><br>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-13pt; padding-left:36pt; text-indent:54pt;  font-size:10pt" align=justify> <b><I>-Hard Commodities Trades:</I></b> iron ore, crude oil, coal, salt, aluminum, copper, gold, silver, palladium and platinum, cement, fly ash, precious metals and other such hard commodities, as intelligence indicates.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=center><B>Completion of Transactions</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><b>Closing Model</b></P>
<P align="left" style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt">Seek out the following results:</P>
<div align="center">
  <TABLE style="font-size:10pt" cellspacing=0>
    <TR><TD width=205.5></TD><TD width=254.25></TD></TR>
    <TR><TD valign=top width=274><P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=center>1. Persistence over the long-run alleviates risk</P>
    </TD><TD valign=top width=339><P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=center>2. Document accumulation creates a ratchet effect towards absolute finalization of transactions </P>
    </TD></TR>
  </TABLE>
</div>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><BR></P>
<br><br>
<P align="center" style="line-height:13pt; margin:0pt; font-size:11pt; align=center;page-break-before:always">3</P>

<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><BR></P>

<div align="center"><BR>
  </P>
  <TABLE style="font-size:10pt" cellspacing=0>
    <TR><TD width=201></TD><TD width=267></TD></TR>
  <TR><TD valign=top width=268><P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><img src="soumtest002.jpg" alt="[soumtest002.jpg" align=middle height=302.8 width=258></P>
  </TD><TD valign=top width=356><P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=center><img src="soumtest003.jpg" alt="[soumtest003.jpg]" align=middle height=316.067 width=323.733></P>

<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><b>Methodology</b></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:36pt; text-indent:54pt" align=justify>1. Find - Intelligence Department (based upon scouting stage of the hunt)</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:36pt; text-indent:54pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:72pt; text-indent:126pt" align=justify>a. Objectives:</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:108pt; text-indent:198pt" align=justify>i.Record first hand &amp; economic &#147;intelligence&#148;</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:108pt; text-indent:198pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:108pt; text-indent:198pt" align=justify>ii.Pool large groups of &#147;target&#148; prices</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:108pt; text-indent:198pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:108pt; text-indent:198pt" align=justify>iii.Match (i.) &#147;intelligence&#148; &amp; (ii.) - &#147;targets&#148; through the company&#146;s fast computing system (hereafter &#147;Medee&#148;)</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:36pt; text-indent:54pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:36pt; text-indent:54pt" align=justify>2. Filter - Development Department (based upon gathering and isolating stage of the hunt)</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:36pt; text-indent:54pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:72pt; text-indent:126pt" align=justify>a. Objectives:</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:108pt; text-indent:198pt" align=justify>i.Attain due diligence on all matched transactions</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:108pt; text-indent:198pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:108pt; text-indent:198pt" align=justify>ii.Filter a list of the best 16 transactions</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:108pt; text-indent:198pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:108pt; text-indent:198pt" align=justify>iii.Attain binding agreements for all parties </P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:36pt; text-indent:54pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:36pt; text-indent:54pt" align=justify>3. Close - Solutions Department (based upon killing stage of the hunt)</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:72pt; text-indent:126pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:72pt; text-indent:126pt" align=justify>a. Objectives:</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:108pt; text-indent:198pt" align=justify>i.Create a closing package on best 5 transactions</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:108pt; text-indent:198pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P><br>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt; padding-left:108pt; text-indent:198pt" align=justify>ii.Inspect, deliver and submit closing package to pertinent parties</P><br>
<br><br>
<P align="center" style="line-height:13pt; margin:0pt; font-size:11pt; align=center;page-break-before:always">4</P>

<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=center><B>Pricing Strategy</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=justify>The Company seeks a pricing that offers the average or greater earnings taken from the pool of transactions. Earnings is calculated as the arbitrage existing across national borders, geographic barriers and economic shifts resulting from political activity or force majeure. </P>
<P style="margin-top:4.6pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt">Since the Company is not building a supply chain it believes the following:</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:10pt; padding-left:36pt; text-indent:54pt;  font-size:10pt">- It carries much less facilities and labor liability.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:10pt; padding-left:36pt; text-indent:54pt;  font-size:10pt">-It chooses transactions with least capital exposure by utilizing fast computing, discovering minimum costs and maximum exit.</P>


<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:10pt; padding-left:36pt; text-indent:54pt;font-size:10pt">-Its delivered price will normally fall beneath our competitors' using less efficient methods of partnerships and cooperative pricing tactics.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><b>Finding opposing targets and intelligence</b></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=center><img src="soumtest004.jpg" alt="[soumtest004.jpg]" align=middle height=325.2 width=468.067></P>

<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>

<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>The Company's common stock is considered a &quot;penny stock&quot; as defined in the Commission's rules promulgated under the Exchange Act (the &#147;Rules&#148;). The Commission's rules regarding penny stocks impose additional sales practice requirements on broker-dealers who sell such securities to persons other than established customers and accredited investors (generally persons with net worth in excess of $1,000,000, exclusive of residence, or an annual income exceeding $200,000 or $300,000 jointly with their spouse). For transactions covered by the rules, the broker-dealer must make a special suitability determination for the purchaser and receive the purchaser's written agreement to the transaction prior to the sale. Thus the Rules affect the ability of broker-dealers to sell the Company's shares should they wish to do so because of the adverse effect that the Rules have upon liquidity of penny stocks. Unless the transaction is exempt under the Rules, under the Securities Enforcement Remedies and Penny Stock Reform Act of 1990, broker-dealers effecting customer transactions in penny stocks are required to provide their customers with (i) a risk disclosure document; (ii) disclosure of current bid and ask quotations if any; (iii) disclosure of the compensation of the broker-dealer and its sales personnel in the transaction; and (iv) monthly account statements showing the market value of each penny stock held in the customer's account. As a result of the penny stock rules, the market liquidity for the Company's securities may be severely adversely affected by limiting the ability of broker-dealers to sell the Company's securities and the ability of purchasers of the securities to resell them.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt"></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR>
<br><br>
<P align="center" style="line-height:13pt; margin:0pt; font-size:11pt; align=center;page-break-before:always">6</P>

<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><BR>
<B>Dividends</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>We have not paid any dividends on our common stock to date and do not anticipate that we will be paying dividends in the foreseeable future. Any payment of cash dividends on our common stock in the future will be dependent upon the amount of funds legally available, our earnings, if any, our financial condition, our anticipated capital requirements and other factors that our Board of Directors may think are relevant. However, we currently intend for the foreseeable future to follow a policy of retaining all of our earnings, if any, to finance the development and expansion of our business and, therefore, do not expect to pay any dividends on our common stock in the foreseeable future. Additionally, the terms of our preferred stock impose restrictions on our ability to pay dividends.</P>

<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><B>Item 7.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;MANAGEMENT&#146;S DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS OF FINANCIAL CONDITION AND RESULTS OF OPERATIONS.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>The following discussion and analysis of financial condition, results of operations, liquidity and capital resources should be read in conjunction with our audited consolidated financial statements and notes thereto appearing elsewhere in this report. This discussion contains forward-looking statements that involve risks and uncertainties, including information with respect to the plans, intentions and strategies for our businesses. <P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><B>Results of Operations</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><B>Year Ended December 31, 2015 Compared With Year Ended December 31, 2014</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>Net revenues for the years ended December 31, 2015 and 2014 was $46,842 and $1,992, respectively. &nbsp;Net income for the year ended December 31, 2015 was $11,023,787 compared to net loss of ($14,751,242) for the year ended December 31, 2014.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>Total operating expenses were $2,003,041 for the year ended December 31, 2015 compared to $1,220,941 for the year ended December 31, 2014. &nbsp;The primary expenses for the year ended December 31, 2015 were general and administrative expenses of $1,338,849, &nbsp;interest expense of approximately $663,192 and compared to general and administrative expenses of $632,478, &nbsp;interest expense of $588,463 for the year ended December 31, 2014. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>Total Other (Income) and Expenses were ($13,022,938) for the year ended December 31, 2015 compared to $13,532,293 for the year ended December 31, 2014. &nbsp;&nbsp;The primary other (income) and expenses for the year ended December 31, 2015 were gain on conversion feature of preferred shares of ($12,845,480) and loss on derivative of $37,878 &nbsp;and write-off of liabilities of $(215,336) compared to loss on conversion feature of preferred shares of $12,845,480, gain on derivative of ($86,998), impairment of goodwill of $480,000 loss on conversion of $293,811 and write off of accrued expenses of $0 for the year ended December 31, 2014.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR>
<br><br>
<P align="center" style="line-height:13pt; margin:0pt; font-size:11pt; align=center;page-break-before:always">7</P>

<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><BR>

<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><B>Liquidity and Capital Resources</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>Our operations used approximately $45,345 in cash for the year ended December 31, 2015. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>Investing activities used $297 for the year ended December 31, 2015. Cash required during the year ended December 31, 2015, came principally from cash proceeds from convertible notes payable of $41,300 and cash proceeds from notes payable affiliates of $4,379.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>Our operations used approximately $180,107 in cash for the year ended December 31, 2014. Cash required during the year ended December 31, 2014, came principally from cash proceeds from debt of $164,500 and cash proceeds from equity purchase agreement of $10,000 for the year ended December 31, 2014.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>The accompanying consolidated financial statements have been prepared assuming that the Company will continue as a going concern, which contemplates the realization of assets and the liquidation of liabilities in the normal course of business. &nbsp;We incurred net income (losses) of $11,022,787 and ($14,751,242), respectively, for the years ended December 31, 2015 and 2014 and had an accumulated deficit of $15,110,830 as of December 31, 2015. &nbsp;We have managed our liquidity during the first, second and third quarters of 2015 through the issuance of convertible notes. &nbsp;These factors raise substantial doubt about the Company&#146;s ability to continue as a going concern. The financial statements do not include any adjustments that might result from the outcome of this uncertainty.</P>

<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><B>Item 9. &nbsp;CONTROLS AND PROCEDURES.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><U>Evaluation of Disclosure Controls and Procedures</U></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><B>&nbsp;</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>Our management, with the participation of our Principal Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer, evaluated the effectiveness of our disclosure controls and procedures (as defined in the Securities Exchange Act of 1934 Rules 13a-15(e) and 15d-15(e)) as of the end of the period covered by this Annual Report on Form 10-K. In designing and evaluating the disclosure controls and procedures, management recognizes that any controls and procedures, no matter how well designed and operated, can provide only reasonable assurance of achieving the desired control objectives. In addition, the design of disclosure controls and procedures must reflect the fact that there are resource constraints and that management is required to apply its judgment in evaluating the benefits of possible controls and procedures relative to their costs.&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>Based on our evaluation, our Principal Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer, after considering the existence of material weaknesses identified, determined that our internal control over financial reporting disclosure controls and procedures were not effective as of December 31, 2015.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><U>Management&#146;s Annual Report on Internal Control over Financial Reporting</U></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>Our management is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporting as defined in Rules 13a-15(f) and 15d-15(f) under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended.&nbsp;&nbsp;Our internal control over financial reporting is designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR>
<br><br>
<P align="center" style="line-height:13pt; margin:0pt; font-size:11pt; align=center;page-break-before:always">8</P>

<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><BR>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>Our internal control over financial reporting includes those policies and procedures that: (i) pertain to the maintenance of records that in reasonable detail accurately and fairly reflect the transactions and dispositions of our assets, (ii) provide reasonable assurance that transactions are recorded as necessary to permit preparation of financial statements in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles, and that our receipts and expenditures are being made only in accordance with the authorization of our management and directors, and (iii) provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition, use or disposition of our assets that could have a material effect on our financial statements.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>Because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements. Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or that the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>Management, including our Principal Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer, assessed the effectiveness of our internal control over financial reporting as of December&nbsp;31, 2015. In making this assessment, management used the criteria set forth by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO) in Internal Control over Financial Reporting - Guidance for Smaller Public Companies.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>We identified the following deficiencies which together constitute a material weakness in our assessment of the effectiveness of internal control over financial reporting as of December 31, 2015:&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:10pt; padding-left:68pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>-The Company has inadequate segregation of duties within its cash disbursement control design.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:72pt" align=justify>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:10pt; padding-left:102pt; text-indent:pt" align=justify>-During the year ended December 31, 2015, the Company internally performed all aspects of its financial reporting process, including, but not limited to the underlying accounting records and the recording of journal entries and for the preparation of financial statements. &nbsp;This process was deficient, because these duties were performed often times by the same people, and therefore a lack of review was created over the financial reporting process that might result in a failure to detect errors in spreadsheets, calculations, or assumptions used to compile the financial statements and related disclosures as filed with the SEC. These control deficiencies could result in a material misstatement to our interim or annual financial statements that would not be prevented or detected. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>The Company is continuing the process of remediating its control deficiencies. However, the material weakness in internal control over financial reporting that has been identified will not be remediated until numerous internal controls are implemented and operate for a period of time, are tested, and the Company is able to conclude that such internal controls are operating effectively. The Company cannot provide assurance that these procedures will be successful in identifying material errors that may exist in the financial statements. The Company cannot make assurances that it will not identify additional material weaknesses in its internal control over financial reporting in the future. Management plans, as capital becomes available to the Company, to increase the accounting and financial reporting staff and provide future investments in the continuing education and public company accounting training of our accounting and financial professionals.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>It should be noted&nbsp;&nbsp;that any&nbsp;&nbsp;system of&nbsp;&nbsp;controls,&nbsp;&nbsp;however&nbsp;&nbsp;well&nbsp;&nbsp;designed&nbsp;&nbsp;and operated,&nbsp;&nbsp;can provide only&nbsp;&nbsp;reasonable,&nbsp;&nbsp;and not absolute,&nbsp;&nbsp;assurance&nbsp;&nbsp;that the objectives of the system are met. In addition, the design of any control system is based in part upon certain assumptions about the likelihood of future events.&nbsp;&nbsp;Because of these and other inherent limitations of control system, there can be no assurance that any design will succeed in achieving its stated goals under all potential future conditions.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>This annual report does not include an attestation report of the Company's registered public accounting firm regarding internal control over financial reporting. Management's report was not subject to attestation by the Company's registered public accounting firm pursuant to rules of the Securities and Exchange Commission that permit us to provide only management's report in this annual report.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR>
<br><br>
<P align="center" style="line-height:13pt; margin:0pt; font-size:11pt; align=center;page-break-before:always">9</P>

<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt"><BR>

<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>We regularly review our system of internal control over financial reporting to ensure we maintain an effective internal control environment. There were no changes in our internal controls over financial reporting during the quarter ended December 31, 2015 that have materially affected, or are reasonably likely to materially affect, our internal control over financial reporting.&nbsp;</P>

<P style="line-height:22pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5.5pt" align=justify><B>BIOGRAPHY</B></P>
<P style="line-height:22pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5.5pt" align=justify>The following sets forth biographical information regarding the Company&#146;s directors:</P>
<P style="line-height:13.5pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=justify><B>William Westbrook </B></P>
<P style="line-height:13.5pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=justify>Since February, 2013 Mr. Westbrook has served as President and CEO, and as a member of the Board of Directors of SoOum. From 2008 to 2013 Mr. Westbrook served as CEO of Estmar Global, Inc. located in West Point, Utah. &nbsp;Estmar Global, Inc. is an international trade company involved in the buying and selling of physical commodities. From 2008 to 2009 Mr. Westbrook served as a business and management consultant for Aspen Technologies, located in Burlington, Massachusetts. &nbsp;From 2007 to 2008 Mr. Westbrook acted as the budget director for Romney for President. William Westbrook served as assistant controller of the Lennar Corporation, located in Tucson, Arizona from 2006 to 2007. In 2001 Mr. Westbrook received a Bachelor of Arts degree in Economics from Brigham Young University, located in Provo, Utah.</P>
<P style="line-height:13.5pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=justify><B>Ronald A. Vega</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13.5pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:8.35pt" align=justify>Mr. Ronald A. Vega served as a Senior Indirect Tax Manager for BP Corporation located in Houston, Texas from March, 2004 through May, 2012. From June, 2012 through February, 2014 Mr. Vega served as Vice President of Business Development for DL Trading, LLC located in Katy, Texas. DL Trading, LLC is involved in the trading of previously undeveloped duty drawback recoveries associated with the importation and exportation of specific petro chemicals, plastics and chemical products. From June, 2013 to the present Mr. Vega was employed by Stelle Innovations, LLC as Vice President of Business Development and Operations. Stelle Innovations, LLC is located in Rye, New York and it is a provider of procurement and sourcing supply chain logistic services for companies engaged in capital improvement projects. From April, 2014 to the present Mr. Vega has served as the Chief Financial Officer and a Director of SoOum Corporation. &nbsp;In 1991, Mr. Vega received a BBA degree in Accounting from the University of Texas-Pan American located in Edinburgh, Texas. In May, 2000 Mr. Vega received a Juris Doctorate Degree from Indiana University School of Law, located in Indianapolis, Indiana. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR>
<br><br>
<P align="center" style="line-height:13pt; margin:0pt; font-size:11pt; align=center;page-break-before:always; margin-bottom: 9.15pt;">10

<P style="line-height:13.5pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=justify><B>Luis J. Vega</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13.5pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt" align=justify>Mr. Luis J. Vega served in the United States Army from 1985 to 2005 as a Nuclear Biological Chemical Warfare Specialist Senior Procurement and Operations manager. From June 2005 to October 2007 Mr. Vega was an employee of SMI GMS at Fort Polk, LA as Senior Logistics Manager assisting deploying military units. From 2007 to August 2009 Mr. Vega was Business Development Manager of Estmar Global. From August, 2009 to October, 2010 Mr. Vega was a Civil Service Employee for the Department of Defense (DOD) and with Cubic Defense Applications located in Ft. Irwin, California, where he was in charge of Middle East, Europe and Asia operations. Cubic Defense Applications is a DOD contractor, and Mr. Vega served as a Training Analyst there. From December, 2010 to August, 2011 Mr. Vega was also employed by ConsultNet which is located in Salt Lake City, Utah. ConsultNet is a staffing and recruiting business, and Mr. Vega served as a recruiter. From 2014, to the present Mr. Vega has served as Chief Operations Officer and a member of the Board of Directors of SoOum. Mr. Vega received a Bachelor of Science degree in Health and Administration from the University of Phoenix in 2011. The University of Phoenix is located in Phoenix, Arizona. In December 2014, he received his Master&#146;s Degree in Health Administration from the University of Phoenix, located in Salt Lake City, Utah. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><B>Corporate Governance</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>The Company promotes accountability for adherence to honest and ethical conduct; endeavors to provide full, fair, accurate, timely and understandable disclosure in reports and documents that the Company files with the Securities and Exchange Commission (the &#147;SEC&#148;) and in other public communications made by the Company; and strives to be compliant with applicable governmental laws, rules and regulations. The Company has not formally adopted a written code of business conduct and ethics that governs the Company&#146;s employees, officers and directors as the Company is not required to do so.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; margin-bottom: -12pt;" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>In lieu of an Audit Committee, the Company&#146;s Board of Directors, is responsible for reviewing and making recommendations concerning the selection of outside auditors, reviewing the scope, results and effectiveness of the annual audit of the Company's financial statements and other services provided by the Company&#146;s independent public accountants. The Board of Directors reviews the Company's internal accounting controls, practices and policies.&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><I>Committees of the Board</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>Our Company currently does not have nominating, compensation, or audit committees or committees performing similar functions nor does the Company have a written nominating, compensation or audit committee charter. The Board of Directors believes that it is not necessary to have such committees, at this time, because the functions of such committees can be adequately performed by the directors.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><I>Audit Committee Financial Expert</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>Our Board of Directors has determined that we do not have a board member that qualifies as an &quot;<U>audit committee financial expert</U> &quot; as defined in Item 407(D)(5) of Regulation S-K, nor do we have a Board member that qualifies as &quot;<U>independent</U>&quot; as the term is used in Item 7(d)(3)(iv)(B) of Schedule 14A under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended, and as defined by Rule 4200(a)(14) of the FINRA Rules.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt; margin-bottom: 9.15pt;" align=justify>We believe that our directors are capable of analyzing and evaluating our financial statements and understanding internal controls and procedures for financial reporting. In addition, we believe that retaining an independent director who would qualify as an &quot;<U>audit committee financial expert</U>&quot; would be overly costly and burdensome and is not warranted in our circumstances given the stage of our development. &nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><I>Board Meetings and Annual Meeting</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><B>&nbsp;</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>During the fiscal year ended December 31, 2015, our Board of Directors held four formal meetings.&nbsp;&nbsp;We did not hold an annual meeting in 2014.&nbsp;&nbsp;All of our directors attended at least 75% of the meetings of the Board of Directors.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><I>Code Of Business Conduct And Ethics</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>Each of the Company&#146;s directors and employees, including its executive officers, are required to conduct themselves in accordance with ethical standards set forth in the Code of Business Conduct and Ethics adopted by the Board of Directors.&nbsp;&nbsp;The Code of Business Conduct and Ethics was previously filed as Exhibit 14.1 to the Company&#146;s Annual Report on Form 10-KSB for the fiscal year ended December 31, 2005. Any amendments to or waivers from the code will be posted on our website.&nbsp;&nbsp;Information on our website does not constitute part of this filing.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR>
<br><br>
<P align="center" style="line-height:13pt; margin:0pt; font-size:11pt; align=center;page-break-before:always; margin-bottom: 9.15pt;">11</P>

<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><I>Shareholder Proposals</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>Our Company does not have any defined policy or procedural requirements for shareholders to submit recommendations or nominations for directors. The Board of Directors believes that, given the stage of our development, a specific nominating policy would be premature and of little assistance until our business operations develop to a more advanced level. Our Company does not currently have any specific or minimum criteria for the election of nominees to the Board of Directors and we do not have any specific process or procedure for evaluating such nominees. The Board of Directors will assess all candidates, whether submitted by management or shareholders, and make recommendations for election or appointment to the Board.</P>

<P style="line-height:13.5pt; margin-top:9.15pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>The Company has no employment contracts. &nbsp;There are no compensation plans or arrangements, including payments to be made by us with respect to our officers, directors, employees or consultants that would result from the resignation, retirement or any other termination of such directors, officers, employees or consultants. There are no arrangements for compensation to be paid to our directors, officers, employees or consultants that would result from a change-in-control.</P>

<P style="margin:0pt"><B>Item 12.&nbsp;SECURITY OWNERSHIP OF CERTAIN BENEFICIAL OWNERS AND MANAGEMENT AND RELATED STOCKHOLDER MATTERS.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>The following table sets forth certain information as of March 31, 2016 with respect to the beneficial ownership of our common stock, by (i) each stockholder known to be the beneficial owner of 5% or more of the outstanding common stock of the Company (based solely on the Company&#146;s record shareholders list as of March 15, 2016, and Schedule 13D&#146;s and Section 16 reports filed with the SEC), (ii) each executive officer and director, and (iii) all executive officers and directors as a group.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>Beneficial ownership has been determined in accordance with Rule 13d-3 under the Exchange Act. Under this rule, certain shares may be deemed to be beneficially owned by more than one person (if, for example, persons share the power to vote or the power to dispose of the shares).&nbsp;&nbsp;In addition, shares are deemed to be beneficially owned by a person if the person has the right to acquire shares (for example, upon exercise of an option or warrant) within 60 days of the date as of which the information is provided. In computing the percentage ownership of any person, the amount of shares is deemed to include the amount of shares beneficially owned by such person by reason of such acquisition rights. As a result, the percentage of outstanding shares of any person as shown in the following table does not necessarily reflect the person&#146;s actual voting power at any particular date.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt; margin-bottom: 9.15pt;" align=left>We believe that, except as otherwise noted and subject to applicable community property laws, each person named in the following table has sole investment and voting power with respect to the shares of common stock shown as beneficially owned by such person.
<BR>
<BR></P>

<P style="line-height:22pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5.5pt"><B><U>SECTION 16(A) BENEFICIAL OWNERSHIP REPORTING COMPLIANCE</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt; margin-bottom: 9.15pt;" align=left>Section&nbsp;16(a) of the Exchange Act requires the Company's directors and officers, and persons who beneficially own more than 10% of a registered class of the Company's equity securities, to file reports of beneficial ownership and changes in beneficial ownership of the Company's securities with the SEC on Forms 3, 4 and 5. Officers, directors and greater than 10% stockholders are required by SEC regulations to furnish the Company with copies of all Section&nbsp;16(a) forms they file.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt; margin-bottom: 9.15pt;" align=left>Based solely on the Company's review of the copies of the forms received by it during the fiscal year ended December&nbsp;31, 2015 and written representations that no other reports were required, the Company does not believe that any persons required to make filings under Section 16(a) during such fiscal year failed to file such reports or filed such reports late. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt"><B>Item 13.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;CERTAIN RELATIONSHIPS, RELATED TRANSACTIONS, AND DIRECTOR INDEPENDENCE.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt"><B>&nbsp;</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt"><B>Review, Approval and Ratification of Related Party Transactions</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt"><B>&nbsp;</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>Given our small size and limited financial resources, we have not adopted formal policies and procedures for the review, approval or ratification of related party transactions, with our executive officers, directors and significant stockholders.&nbsp;&nbsp;We intend to establish formal policies and procedures in the future, once we have sufficient resources and have appointed additional directors, so that such transactions will be subject to the review, approval or ratification of our Board of Directors, or an appropriate committee thereof.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On a moving forward basis, our directors will continue to approve any related party transaction.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><B>&nbsp;</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt"><B>Director Independence</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt; margin-bottom: 9.15pt;" align=justify>We do not have an audit, compensation or nominating committee, but our entire Board of Directors acts in such capacities.&nbsp;&nbsp;Although our directors are not considered as &#147;independent directors&#148; pursuant to the provisions of Item 407(a) of Regulation S-K, we believe that the members of our Board of Directors are capable of analyzing and evaluating our financial statements and understanding internal controls and procedures for financial reporting.&nbsp;&nbsp;The Board of Directors of our Company does not believe that it is necessary to have an audit committee, because we believe that the functions of an audit committee can be adequately performed by the Board of Directors.&nbsp;&nbsp;In addition, we believe that retaining an independent director who would qualify as an &#147;audit committee financial expert&#148; would be overly costly and burdensome and is not warranted in our circumstances given the early stage of our development.&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P style="margin:0pt"><B>Pre-Approval Policy for Services of SoOum Financial Independent Auditors</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt" align=justify>The Board of Directors review the Form 10-Q and Form 10-K filings before their filing.&nbsp;In addition, the Board of Directors reviews the audit plans and anticipated fees for audit and tax work prior to the commencement of that work.&nbsp;All fees paid to the independent auditors are pre-approved by the Board of Directors.&nbsp;These services may include audit services, audit-related services, tax services and other services.&nbsp;</P>

<P style="line-height:14.65pt; margin-top:3.45pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt; font-size:11pt" align=center><B>REPORT OF INDEPENDENT REGISTERED PUBLIC ACCOUNTING FIRM</B></P>
<P style="line-height:14.65pt; margin-top:3.45pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt; font-size:11pt" align=center>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="line-height:14.65pt; margin-top:3.45pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt; font-size:11pt" align=center><FONT COLOR=#3F3F3F>Scrudato &amp; Co., PA</FONT></P>
<P align="center" style="line-height:14pt; margin:0pt; font-size:12pt; color:#3F3F3F">CERTIFIED PUBLIC ACCOUNTING FIRM</P>
<P style="margin:0pt"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14.65pt; margin-top:3.45pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt; font-size:11pt"><FONT COLOR=#000000>To the Board of Directors and Stockholders of
SoOum Holdings, Corp.</FONT></P>
<P style="line-height:14.65pt; margin-top:3.45pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt; font-size:11pt" align=justify>We have audited the accompanying balance sheets of SoOum Holdings, Corp. as of December 31, 2015 and 2014 and the related consolidated statements of operations, changes in stockholders&#146; deficit and cash flows for the years then ended. These financial statements are the responsibility of the Company management. Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements based on our audit.</P>
<P style="line-height:14.65pt; margin-top:3.45pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt; font-size:11pt" align=justify>We conducted our audit in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States). Those standards require that we plan and perform the audits to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the consolidated financial statements are free of material misstatement. The Company is not required to have, nor were we engaged to perform, an audit of its internal control over financial reporting. Our audits included consideration of internal control over financial reporting as a basis for designing audit procedures that are appropriate in the circumstances, but not for the purpose of expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of the Company&#146;s internal control over financial reporting. Accordingly, we express no such opinion. An audit also includes examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the consolidated financial statements, assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall financial statement presentation. We believe that our audit provide a reasonable basis for our opinion.</P>
<P style="line-height:14.65pt; margin-top:3.45pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt; font-size:11pt" align=justify>In our opinion, the financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of SoOum Holdings, Corp. at December 31, 2015 and 2014, and the results of their operations and their cash flows for the the years then ended in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America.</P>
<P style="line-height:14.65pt; margin-top:3.45pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The accompanying financial statements have been prepared assuming that SoOum Holdings, Corp. will continue as a going concern. As more fully described in Note D, the Company had an accumulated deficit at December 31, 2015, a net loss and net cash used in operating activities for the fiscal year then ended. These conditions raise substantial doubt about the ability of the Company to continue as a going concern. Management&#146;s plans in regards to these matters are also described in Note D. The financial statements do not include any adjustments to reflect the possible future effects on the recoverability and classification of assets or the amounts and classification of liabilities that may result from the outcome of this uncertainty.</P>
<P style="line-height:14.65pt; margin-top:3.45pt; margin-bottom:9.15pt; font-size:11pt">

/s/ John Scrudato CPA

<P align="center" style="line-height:13pt; margin:0pt; font-size:11pt; align=center;page-break-before:always; margin-bottom: 0pt;">21</P>

<P style="margin:0pt">&nbsp;</P>





<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR></P>
<P align="center" style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman"><B>SOOUM CORP.</B></P>
<P align="center" style="margin:0pt; font-family:new times roman"><FONT FACE="new times roman"><B>New York, New York</B></FONT></P>
<P align="center" style="margin:0pt; font-family:new times roman">&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; padding-bottom:3pt; text-indent:-45.35pt; font-family:new times roman; border-bottom:2.25pt solid #000000" align=center><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>

<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:30.8pt; text-indent:-30.8pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><FONT FACE="times new roman"><B>NOTE A &#150; The Company</B></FONT></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-14pt; padding-left:48.25pt; text-indent:-48.25pt; font-size:12pt" align=justify><FONT FACE="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-size:10pt" align=justify><FONT FACE="times new roman">The Company &#147;SoOum Corp.&#148;, formerly known as</FONT> <FONT FACE="times new roman">Swordfish Financial, Inc., (a Texas Corporation) (the &#147;Company&#148;), acquired 80% of the outstanding common stock of Nature Vision, Inc. pursuant to a stock acquisition/merger agreement on August 14, 2009. &nbsp;Based a on a review of these factors, the August 2009 stock acquisition agreement with Swordfish Financial, Inc., the merger was accounted for as a reverse acquisition (i.e. Nature Vision, Inc. was considered as the acquired company and Swordfish Financial, Inc., was considered as the acquiring company). &nbsp;As a result, Nature Vision, Inc.&#146;s assets and liabilities as of August 14, 2009, the date of the Merger closing, have been incorporated into Swordfish&#146;s balance sheet based on the fair values of the net assets acquired. &nbsp;Further, the Company&#146;s operating results (post-Merger) include Swordfish Financial, Inc., operating results prior to the date of closing and the results of the combined entity following the closing of the Merger. Also as a result of the merger the Company changed its name from Nature Vision to Swordfish Financial, Inc.</FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><FONT FACE="times new roman">On September 23, 2014 the Company entered into a Securities Purchase Agreement with 100% of the common stock shareholders (the &#147;Sellers&#148;) of SoOum Corp. &nbsp;Upon the closing of the transaction on November 10, 2014, SoOum Corp. shareholders transferred all of their outstanding shares of common stock to SoOum Holdings, Inc., a wholly owned subsidiary of Swordfish. &nbsp;In consideration, Swordfish issued 9,100,000 shares of its Class B Preferred stock and 1,690,000 shares of its Class C preferred Stock. &nbsp;The Class B Preferred Stock is convertible at the rate of 1 common shares to 1. &nbsp;The Class C Preferred Stock is convertible at the rate of 10 common shares to 1. &nbsp;Class B and Class C have voting rights of 1,000 to 1 per share. Also as a result of the merger the Company changed its name from Swordfish Financial, Inc., to SoOum Corp.</FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><B>Nature of Operations</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><B></B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>Swordfish Financial, Inc., (f/k/a Nature Vision, Inc. and Photo Control Corporation) as Nature Vision, Inc. previously designed, manufactured and marketed outdoor recreation products primarily for the sport fishing and hunting markets.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>The Company did not meet the minimum net worth covenants of a line of credit with M&amp;I Business Credit LLC (M&amp;I Bank) as of June 30, 2009, which put the Company in default on the line of credit. &nbsp;On August 14, 2009, simultaneously with the signing of the Swordfish Financial, Inc., the Texas corporation, stock Purchase/Merger Agreement (described above) M&amp;I Bank, which was owed approximately $1,800,000 by the Company, foreclosed on the line of credit and forced the Company to enter into a Voluntary Surrender Agreement. &nbsp;The Voluntary Surrender Agreement gave M&amp;I Bank total possession of the Company&#146;s premises, its operations and all of the Company&#146;s collateral, which consisted of all of Nature Vision&#146;s assets. &nbsp;M&amp;I Bank liquidated basically all of the Nature Vision assets to recover the line of credit debt. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=center><BR></P>

</P>
<P align="center" style="line-height:13pt; margin:0pt; font-size:11pt; align=center;page-break-before:always; margin-bottom: 0pt;">22</P><br>

<P style="margin:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<P align="center" style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman"><B>SOOUM CORP.</B></P>
<P align="center" style="margin:0pt; font-family:new times roman"><FONT FACE="new times roman"><B>New York, New York</B></FONT></P>
<P align="center" style="margin:0pt; font-family:new times roman">&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; padding-bottom:3pt; text-indent:-45.35pt; font-family:new times roman; border-bottom:2.25pt solid #000000" align=center><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:30.8pt; text-indent:-30.8pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><FONT FACE="times new roman"><B>NOTE A &#150; The Company &#150; continued</B></FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:30.8pt; text-indent:-30.8pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>Based on the limited assets, product lines and resources remaining after the M&amp;I Bank liquidation, the Company determined that there was not enough remaining of the Nature Vision operations to continue as an outdoor recreation product company and decided to concentrate on the business on being an asset recovery company and using the financial resources recovered to retire the Company&#146;s debts and invest in other businesses domestically and internationally.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;Effective approximately December 2012, the Company decided to discontinue its efforts on being an asset recovery company and changed its business focus to the pursuit of the acquisition of Internet media companies which provide service to home entertainment and cable business.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>Effective with the merger of SoOum Corp., the Company changed its business focus to international commodity trading arbitrage. &nbsp;The Company will use its own proprietary technology to identify and exploit arbitrage opportunities. &nbsp;SoOum also plans to distribute trade intelligence to global subscribers in order to solve supply shortages and bring new business to local manufacturers.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><B>Principles of Consolidation</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>The consolidated financial statements include the accounts of SoOum Corp., and its wholly owned subsidiaries; Nature Vision, Inc. and SoOum (the &#147;Company&#148;). &nbsp;All significant inter-company balances have been eliminated in consolidation.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>

<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><B>NOTE B &#150; Summary of Significant Accounting Policies</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><B>Method of Accounting</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:99pt; text-indent:-99pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>The Company maintains its books and prepares its financial statements on the accrual &nbsp;basis of accounting.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; text-indent:-0.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; text-indent:-0.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;<B>Cash and Cash Equivalents</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; text-indent:-0.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><B>&nbsp;</B>Cash and cash equivalents include time deposits, certificates of deposit, and all highly &nbsp;&nbsp;liquid debt instruments with original maturities of three months or less. &nbsp;The Company &nbsp;&nbsp;maintains cash and cash equivalents at financial institutions, which periodically may&nbsp;exceed federally insured amounts. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><B>Income Taxes</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>The Company accounts for income taxes in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles which prescribes the use of the liability method whereby deferred tax asset and liability account balances are determined based on differences between the financial reporting and tax bases of assets and liabilities and are measured using the enacted tax rates and laws that will be in effect when the differences are expected to reverse. &nbsp;The Company provides a valuation allowance, if necessary, to reduce deferred tax assets to their estimated realizable value.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=center><BR></P>

</P>
<P align="center" style="line-height:13pt; margin:0pt; font-size:11pt; align=center;page-break-before:always; margin-bottom: 0pt;">23</P>
<br>

<P style="margin:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<P align="center" style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman">S<B>OOUM CORP.</B></P>
<P align="center" style="margin:0pt; font-family:new times roman"><FONT FACE="new times roman"><B>New York, New York</B></FONT></P>
<P align="center" style="margin:0pt; font-family:new times roman">&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; padding-bottom:3pt; text-indent:-45.35pt; font-family:new times roman; border-bottom:2.25pt solid #000000" align=center><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><FONT FACE="times new roman"><B>NOTE B &#150; Summary of Significant Accounting Policies &#150; continued</B></FONT></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-14pt; padding-left:45pt; text-indent:-45pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:43pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;<B>Income Taxes</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>The Company evaluates all significant tax positions as required by accounting principles &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;generally accepted in the United States of America. &nbsp;As of December 31, 2015, the &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Company does not believe that it has taken any positions that would require the recording &nbsp;of any additional tax liability nor does it believe that there are any unrealized tax benefits &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that would either increase or decrease within the next year. &nbsp;It is the Company&#146;s policy to &nbsp;&nbsp;recognize any interest and penalties in the provision for taxes.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><b>Earnings per Share</b></B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>Earnings per share of common stock are computed in accordance with FASB ASC 260 (prior authoritative literature: &nbsp;FASB Statement No. 128.), FASB ASC 260 replaces SFAS No, 128, &#147;Earnings per Share&#148;.&nbsp;&nbsp;Basic earnings per share are computed by dividing income or loss available to common shareholders by the weighted-average number of common shares outstanding for each period.&nbsp;&nbsp;Diluted earnings per share are calculated by adjusting the weighted average number of shares outstanding assuming conversion of all potentially dilutive stock options, warrants and convertible securities, if dilutive. Common stock equivalents that are anti-dilutive are excluded from both diluted weighted average number of common shares outstanding and diluted earnings per share.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><b>Financial Instruments</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>The Company&#146;s financial instruments consist of cash, long-term investments, and accounts payable. Unless otherwise noted, it is management&#146;s opinion that the Company is not exposed to significant interest, currency or credit risks arising from these financial instruments. &nbsp;The fair value of these financial instruments approximates their carrying value, unless otherwise noted.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><B>Stock-Based Compensation</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:49.5pt; text-indent:-45pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>Stock-based compensation is computed in accordance with FASB ASC 718 (prior authoritative literature: &nbsp;FASB Statement No. 123R). FASB ASC 718 replaces SFAS No. 123R which requires all share-based payment to employees, including grants of employee stock options, to be recognized as compensation expense in the financial statements based on their fair values.&nbsp;&nbsp;That expense will be recognized over the period during which an employee is required to provide services in exchange for the award, known as the requisite service period (usually the vesting period). The Company has selected the Black-Scholes option pricing model as the most appropriate fair value method for our awards and have recognized compensation costs immediately as our awards are 100% vested.&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;The Company&#146;s accounting policy for equity instruments issued to consultants and vendors in exchange for goods and services follows the provisions of FASB ASC 505-50 (prior authoritative literature, EITF 96-18, &#147;Accounting for Equity Instruments That are Issued to Other Than Employees for Acquiring, or in Conjunction with Selling, Goods or Services&#148; and EITF 00-18, &#147;Accounting Recognition for Certain Transactions Involving Equity Instruments Granted to Other Than Employees.&#148;) &nbsp;The measurement date for the fair value of the equity instruments issued is determined at the earlier of (i)&nbsp;the date at which a commitment for performance by the consultant or vendor is reached or (ii)&nbsp;the date at which the consultant or vendor&#146;s performance is complete. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=center><BR></P>

</P>
<P align="center" style="line-height:13pt; margin:0pt; font-size:11pt; align=center;page-break-before:always; margin-bottom: 0pt;">24</P>
<br>

<P style="margin:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<P align="center" style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman"><B>SOOUM CORP.</B></P>
<P align="center" style="margin:0pt; font-family:new times roman"><FONT FACE="new times roman"><B>New York, New York</B></FONT></P>
<P align="center" style="margin:0pt; font-family:new times roman">&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; padding-bottom:3pt; text-indent:-45.35pt; font-family:new times roman; border-bottom:2.25pt solid #000000" align=center><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; text-indent:-45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><FONT FACE="times new roman"><B>NOTE B &#150; Summary of Significant Accounting Policies - continued</B></FONT> </P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; text-indent:-45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:41.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><B>Stock-Based Compensation - continued</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>In the case of equity instruments issued to consultants, the fair value of the equity instrument is recognized over the term of the consulting agreement. &nbsp;Stock-based compensation related to non-employees is accounted for based on the fair value of the related stock or options or the fair value of the services, whichever is more readily determinable in accordance with ASC 718. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin:0pt; padding-left:42.5pt; text-indent:; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><B>Use of Estimates</B></P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin:0pt; padding-left:42.5pt; text-indent:; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>The preparation of financial statements in conformity with generally accepted accounting principles in the United States of America requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting period. &nbsp;Actual results could differ from those estimates.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><B>Derivative Financial Instruments</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman">&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>The Company does not use derivative instruments to hedge exposures to cash flow, market or foreign currency risks.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><FONT FACE="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><FONT FACE="times new roman">The Company reviews the terms of the common stock, warrants and convertible debt it issues to determine whether there are embedded derivative instruments, including embedded conversion options, which are required to be bifurcated and accounted for separately as derivative financial instruments.&nbsp;&nbsp;In circumstances where the host instrument contains more than one embedded derivative instrument, including the conversion option, that is required to be bifurcated, the bifurcated derivative instruments are accounted for as a single, compound derivative instrument.</FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>Bifurcated embedded derivatives are initially recorded at fair value and are then revalued at each reporting date with changes in the fair value reported as non-operating income or expense. The Company uses a lattice model for valuation of the derivative. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>When the equity or convertible debt instruments contain embedded derivative instruments that are to be bifurcated and accounted for as liabilities, the total proceeds received are first allocated to the fair value of all the bifurcated derivative instruments.&nbsp;&nbsp;The remaining proceeds, if any, are then allocated to the host instruments themselves, usually resulting in those instruments being recorded at a discount from their face value.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>The discount from the face value of the convertible debt, together with the stated interest on the instrument, is amortized over the life of the instrument through periodic charges to interest expense, using the effective interest method.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>Derivative instrument liabilities are classified in the balance sheet as current or non-current based on whether net cash settlement of the derivative instrument could be required within the 12 months of the balance sheet date.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; page-break-before:always" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; page-break-before:always" align=center>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=center><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><B>NOTE D &#150; Acquisition &#150; iPoint Television</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;On January 15, 2014, the Company completed the acquisition of 90% of the issued and outstanding membership interest of iPoint. &nbsp;Pursuant to the Securities and Exchange Agreement the Company issued Clark Ortiz, the company&#146;s CEO and Chairman 25,000,000 shares of Swordfish&#146;s Series A Preferred Stock, which has voting rights equal to 100 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock and is convertible into the Company&#146;s common stock at the rate of 10 shares of common stock for each share of Series A. Preferred Stock. &nbsp;In addition to issuance of the Series A Preferred Stock the Company agreed as part of the purchase price to issue 50,000,000 shares of its common stock to Mr. Ortiz. &nbsp;At the date of the transaction, the Company didn&#146;t have any authorized and unissued shares available to issue to Mr. Ortiz, however in order to close the transaction, Mr. Ortiz agreed to close the transaction pending the Company increasing the authorized shares of common stock, which the Company did on March 25, 2014. &nbsp;As a result of the transaction, the Company owns 90% of issued and outstanding membership interests in iPoint Television LLC and therefore a majority owned subsidiary of the Company and the Company will be able to report the results of iPoint on a consolidated basis in the Company&#146;s financial statements. &nbsp;iPoint Television, also known as iPoint TV, is a Smart media and entertainment company, which holds development licenses from Apple, Android, Google, Roku, Kindle and most every smart device. &nbsp;iPoint is &nbsp;a full service Internet Protocol Television (IPTV), media entertainment company which develops applications for mobile and TV smart devices. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><FONT FACE="times new roman"><B>NOTE E &#150; Going Concern</B></FONT>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>The Company&#146;s consolidated financial statements have been presented on the basis that it is a going concern, which contemplates the realization of assets and the satisfaction of liabilities in the normal course of business. The Company has reported recurring losses from operations. &nbsp;As a result, there is an accumulated deficit at December 31, 2015.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:48.25pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>The Company&#146;s continued existence is dependent upon its ability to raise capital or acquire a marketable company. &nbsp;The consolidated financial statements do not include any adjustments that might be necessary should the Company be unable to continue as a going concern.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>

<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify><FONT FACE="times new roman"><B>NOTE G &#150; Convertible Promissory Notes Payable</B></FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>As of December 31, 2015, the Company has outstanding eight (8) security purchase agreements with accredited investors for the sale of convertible promissory notes bearing interest at 10% - 12%, per annum. &nbsp;Pursuant to the convertible promissory notes the investor may convert the amount paid towards the Securities Purchase Agreements into common stock of the Company. &nbsp;Conversion prices vary based on the agreements and have various discount rates and terms. Trading price means the closing bid price on the OTC Market Over-the-Counter Bulletin Board Pink Sheets.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>The conversion rights embedded in the Notes are accounted for as derivative financial instruments because of the down round feature of the conversion price. &nbsp;The beneficial conversion feature was valued at the date of issuance using the Black-Scholes-Merton options pricing model with the following assumptions: &nbsp;risk free interest rates ranging from .07% to .45%, contractual expected life of six (6) to twelve (12) months, expected volatility of 185% to 931%, calculated using the historical closing price of the company&#146;s common stock, and dividend yield of zero, resulting in fair market value.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:45.35pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt; font-family:times new roman" align=justify>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company had convertible debentures outstanding as follows:</P>
